<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">5.&nbsp;Capital Stock</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The Company has an authorized class of
undesignated preferred stock consisting of 300,000 shares.
Preferred stock may be issued in series from time to time with
such designations, relative rights, priorities, preferences,
qualifications, limitations and restrictions thereof, to the
extent that such are not fixed in the Company&#146;s certificate
of incorporation, as the Board of Directors determines.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On February&nbsp;9, 1996, the Board of Directors
adopted a shareholder rights plan (the &#147;Rights Plan&#148;).
In conjunction with the adoption of the Rights Plan, the Company
created one series of preferred stock, consisting of 10,000
shares of Series&nbsp;A Junior Participating Preferred Stock
(&#147;Series&nbsp;A Preferred&#148;). Each share of
Series&nbsp;A Preferred would entitle the holder to receive
dividends equal to 1,000 times the dividends per share declared
with respect to the Company&#146;s common stock and, in the
event of liquidation, such holders would receive a preference of
1,000 times the aggregate amount to be distributed per share to
the holders of the Company&#146;s common stock. Pursuant to the
Rights Plan, a Series&nbsp;A Right is associated with, and
trades with, each share of common stock outstanding. The record
date for distribution of such Series&nbsp;A Rights was
February&nbsp;22, 1996, and for so long as the Series&nbsp;A
Rights are associated with the common stock, each new share of
common stock issued by the Company will include a Series&nbsp;A
Right. Each Series&nbsp;A Right will entitle its holder to
purchase one&nbsp;one-thousandth of a share of Series&nbsp;A
Preferred for $200, subject to adjustment as defined in the
Rights Plan. The Series&nbsp;A Rights are not exercisable until
the earlier of (i)&nbsp;10&nbsp;days after any person or group
becomes the beneficial owner of 15% or more of the
Company&#146;s outstanding common stock, or (ii)&nbsp;10
business days (unless extended by the Board of Directors) after
the commencement of a tender offer or exchange offer that would
result in a person or group beneficially owning 15% or more of
the Company&#146;s outstanding common stock.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">If any person or group (&#147;Acquiring
Party&#148;) acquires 15% or more of the Company&#146;s
outstanding common stock (&#147;Shares Acquisition Date&#148;),
each holder of a Series&nbsp;A Right, except the Acquiring
Party, has the right to receive upon exercise (i)&nbsp;shares of
the Company&#146;s common stock having a market value equal to
two times the exercise price of the Series&nbsp;A Right, and
(ii)&nbsp;one Series&nbsp;B Right (Series&nbsp;A Rights and
Series&nbsp;B Rights are hereinafter collectively referred to as
the &#147;Rights&#148;). The Board of Directors has the option,
after the Shares Acquisition Date but before there has been a
50% acquisition of the Company, to exchange one&nbsp;share of
common stock (or one&nbsp;one-thousandth of a share of preferred
stock) and one Series&nbsp;B Right for each Series&nbsp;A Right
(other than Series&nbsp;A Rights held by the Acquiring Party).
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">If, after the Series&nbsp;A Rights become
exercisable, the Company is involved in a merger or other
business combination, or if the Company sells or transfers more
than 50% of its assets or earning power, or if an acquiring
party engages in
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">6.&nbsp;Stock Options and Warrants</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On August&nbsp;19, 1993, the Board of Directors
adopted the 1993 Stock Option Plan (the &#147;Plan&#148;) for
employees, consultants, and directors who are not also employees
of the Company (outside directors). The maximum number of shares
issuable under the Plan, as amended, in 2002 was 14,011,468. The
Plan is administered by a committee (the &#147;Committee&#148;)
consisting of two or more outside directors appointed by the
board of directors of the Company.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">For employees and consultants, the Plan provides
for granting of Incentive Stock Options (ISOs) and Nonstatutory
Stock Options (NSOs). In the case of ISOs, the exercise price
shall not be less than 100% (110% in certain cases) of the fair
value of the Company&#146;s common stock, as determined by the
Committee, on the date of grant. In the case of NSOs, the
exercise price shall not be less than 25% (110% in certain
cases) of the fair value of the Company&#146;s common stock, as
determined by the Committee, on the date of grant. The term of
options granted to employees and consultants will be for a
period not to exceed 10&nbsp;years (five&nbsp;years in certain
cases). Options granted under the Plan generally vest over a
four&nbsp;year period (one-fourth of options granted vest after
one&nbsp;year from the grant date and the remaining options vest
ratably each month thereafter). In addition, the Committee may
authorize option grants with vesting provisions that are not
based solely on employees&#146; rendering of additional service
to the Company.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">For outside directors, NSOs only will be granted
with an exercise price of 100% of the fair value of the stock,
as determined by the Committee, on the date of grant. The Plan
provides that each outside director will be automatically
granted 40,000 NSOs on the date of their initial election to the
board of directors. On the date of the annual meeting of the
stockholders of the Company, each outside director who is
elected, reelected, or continues to serve as a director, shall
be granted 40,000 NSOs, except for those outside directors who
are first elected to the Board of Directors at the meeting or
three months prior. The options granted vest ratably over two
years and expire after ten years from the grant date.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The Company entered into stock option agreements
with certain employees and a consultant prior to the adoption of
the Plan. These stock options expire 10&nbsp;years from the date
of grant. Exercise prices were determined by the Board of
Directors and represented estimated fair values of the
Company&#146;s common stock at the grant date.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On May&nbsp;10, 1999, the Board of Directors
granted to each employee of the Company (other than the
executive officers of the Company) (collectively, the
&#147;Non-Executive Employees&#148;) the option to
(i)&nbsp;reduce the exercise prices of
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">up to a maximum of 15,000 of the unexercised
stock options previously granted to such Non-Executive Employee
under the Plan to $.5625 per share (the closing price of the
Company&#146;s Common Stock on May&nbsp;10, 1999) and
(ii)&nbsp;cause all of such stock options not otherwise

to become fully vested on such date. As a result thereof, an
aggregate of 279,550 stock options previously granted under the

addition, on May&nbsp;10, 1999 the Board of Directors granted to
the executive officers and certain Non-Executive Employees of
the Company additional non-statutory stock options to purchase
an aggregate of 343,575 shares of the Company&#146;s Common
Stock under the Plan. Such stock options became fully vested on

of $.5625 per share and expire 10&nbsp;years from the date of
grant.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On July&nbsp;1, 2000, Financial Accounting
Standards Board Interpretation No.&nbsp;44, &#147;Accounting for
Certain Transactions involving Stock Compensation, an
interpretation of APB Opinion No.&nbsp;25&#148;
(&#147;FIN&nbsp;44&#148;) was adopted by the Company.
FIN&nbsp;44 requires that stock options that have been modified
to reduce the exercise price be subject to variable accounting.
The Company accounts for employee stock options under APB
Opinion No.&nbsp;25 and non-employee stock options under
Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;123,
&#147;Accounting for Stock Based Compensation&#148; (&#147;SFAS
No.&nbsp;123&#148;).
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On May&nbsp;10, 1999, as described above, the
Company re-priced certain stock options granted to employees and
in accordance with US GAAP, at that time, the Company accounted
for the re-priced stock options as &#147;fixed&#148;. As a
result of adopting FIN&nbsp;44, the Company is required to apply
variable accounting to these options. If the market price of the
Company&#146;s common stock increases above the July&nbsp;1,
2000 market price, the Company will have to recognize additional
compensation expense equal to the increase in stock price
multiplied by the number of re-priced options. No additional
expense will be recognized if the stock does not exceed the
July&nbsp;1, 2000 value. However, the impact cannot be
determined as it is dependent on the change in the market price
of the common stock from July&nbsp;1, 2000 until the stock
options are exercised, forfeited, or expire unexercised. Because
the stock price on December&nbsp;31, 2002 was below that of
July&nbsp;1, 2000, no expense has been recognized during the
period.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On February&nbsp;5, 2001, the Company&#146;s
board of directors authorized the re-pricing of certain
&#147;out of the money&#148; stock options granted to employees
during the calendar year of 2000 to the closing share price on
such date, or $1.9375 per share. Options for a total of
2,676,000 shares of common stock were affected. This re-pricing
causes these options to be subject to variable accounting as
described in FIN 44. Because the stock price on
December&nbsp;31, 2002, was lower than the re-priced strike
price no gain or loss was recognized during the period.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On April&nbsp;1, 2002, the Company&#146;s board
of directors authorized the re-pricing of certain &#147;out of
the money&#148; stock options granted to employees. A new strike
price of $0.81 per share was established, provided the
respective employees remain with the Company for at least six
months following the re-pricing date. In addition, certain stock
options granted to directors were repriced, with a new strike
price of $1.00 per share. As the stock price on
December&nbsp;31, 2002, was lower than the re-priced strike
price no gain or loss was recognized during the period.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On July&nbsp;17, 2000, the Company granted an
option to a non-Company advisor in connection with the
establishment of a sales office in Japan to purchase 200,000
shares of common stock at $4.9375 per share, the price of the
common stock on the date of the grant. According to the
Black-Scholes valuation model, the value of the option was $4.53
per share. The option vested 25% immediately, with the balance
vesting pro-rata over a three-year period. $906,000 of non-cash
compensation expense was to be amortized during the life of the
options. This arrangement was terminated during
December&nbsp;2001, as a result of a change in the structure of
the Japanese sales office. The cumulative compensation expense
charged for these services through termination was $545,000.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On February&nbsp;15, 2000, the Company&#146;s
board of directors granted to certain executive level employees
an aggregate of 440,000 deferred stock units (&#147;DSUs&#148;)
under the Company&#146;s 1993 Amended and Restated Stock Option
Plan (the &#147;Plan&#148;). The DSU&#146;s represent the right
to receive an equivalent number of restricted shares of the
Company&#146;s common stock. On the date of the grant, the
DSU&#146;s were set to vest at the rate of 10% on the first
anniversary of the date of the grant, with the balance vesting
at a rate of 20%, 30%, and 40% at the second, third, and fourth
anniversary dates, respectively. The executive level employees
had the right to elect to defer receipt of the common stock
subject to the
</FONT>

</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">During 2002, the Company&#146;s Board of
Directors granted 2,172,000 new stock options to the
Company&#146;s employees, including officers (option prices are
generally, but not always, set at the closing price of the
Company&#146;s common stock as of the date of each respective
grant). Those grants include the issuance of 900,000 stock
options to the CEO during December, 2002 that vest immediately
and are priced at a $0.20 discount to the closing price of the
Company&#146;s common stock as of the date of grant.
Consequently, $180,000 of compensation expense was recognized
during December, 2002, in order to account for this discount. On
January&nbsp;2, 2003, the Company&#146;s Board of Directors
granted 2,800,000 new stock options to six of the Company&#146;s
employees, including officers. 950,000 of these options vested
immediately, while the remaining 1,850,000 vest monthly in 12
installments. All of the options granted on January&nbsp;2, 2003
were granted at a $0.22 discount to the closing price of the
Company&#146;s common stock as of the date of the grant.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On February&nbsp;15, 2002, the Company completed
a Shareholder Rights Offering. Approximately $20&nbsp;million
was raised from existing shareholders as of the recording date
in exchange for the issuance of approximately 40&nbsp;million
shares of the Company&#146;s common stock. A portion of the
proceeds were then used to repay in full $9.8&nbsp;million of
debt and related accrued interest, as well as the payment of
various other accrued expenses.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Pro forma information regarding net income and
earnings per share is required under FASB&nbsp;123, and has been
determined as if the Company had accounted for its stock options
granted subsequent to December&nbsp;31, 1994 under the fair
value method of that Statement. The fair value for these options
was estimated at the date of grant using a Black-Scholes option
pricing model with the following weighted-average assumptions
for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2002, 2001 and 2000:
risk-free interest rate of 2.9%, 4.2%, and 5.1%, respectively; a
dividend yield of 0%; volatility factor of the expected market
price of the Company&#146;s common stock of 0.15, 0.56, and
2.33, respectively; and expected life of the options of
4.0&nbsp;years.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The Black-Scholes option valuation model was
developed for use in estimating the fair value of traded options
which have no vesting restrictions and are fully transferable.
In addition, option valuation models require the input of highly
subjective assumptions, including the expected stock price
volatility. Because the Company&#146;s employee stock options
have characteristics significantly different from those of
traded options, and because changes in the subjective input
assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate, in
management&#146;s opinion, the existing models do not
necessarily provide a reliable single measure of the fair value
of its employee stock options.
</FONT>

<FONT size="2">The weighted-average exercise price of options
outstanding at December&nbsp;31, 2002, 2001 and 2000, was $0.96,
1.64, and 2.97, respectively. The weighted-average exercise
price of options granted, exercised, and forfeited during 2002
was $0.40, $0.00 and $1.20, respectively. The weighted-average
fair value of options granted during 2002, 2001 and 2000 was
$0.18, $1.52, and $3.86, respectively.
</FONT>

<B><FONT size="2">NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL
STATEMENTS&nbsp;&#151;&nbsp;(Continued)</FONT></B>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">7.&nbsp;Long-Term Debt</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">As of the reporting date, the Company had drawn
$2&nbsp;million of debt financing under a credit line. During
October&nbsp;2002, the Company entered into an Uncommitted Line
of Credit with its two largest shareholders, an affiliate of
Elliott Associates, L.P. (Manchester Securities Corporation and
Alexander Finance, L.P. This line is intended to provide up to
$4&nbsp;million to the Company. This line is uncommitted, such
that each new borrowing under the facility would be subject to
the approval of the lenders. Borrowings on this line bear an
interest rate of 9.5% and are collateralized by all the assets
of the Company. Outstanding loans under this agreement would be
required to be repaid on a priority basis should the Company
receive new funding from other sources. Additionally, the
lenders are entitled to receive warrants to the extent funds are
drawn down on the line. The warrants bear a strike price of
$0.20 per share of common stock and expire on April&nbsp;15,
2004. The credit line matures and is due, including accrued
interest thereon, on March&nbsp;31, 2004. Warrants to purchase
10&nbsp;million shares of common stock were issued in connection
with the borrowings under the line of credit during the year
ended December&nbsp;31, 2002.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">According to existing accounting pronouncements
and SEC guidelines, the Company has allocated the proceeds of
these borrowings between their debt and equity components. As a
result of these borrowings during 2002, the Company will record
a non-cash charge of $1.2&nbsp;million through the outstanding
term of the warrants (April, 2004). $128,000 of that amount was
recorded during 2002.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">Subject to its ability to draw the remaining
$1&nbsp;million from the uncommitted line of credit, the Company
believes that it has sufficient funds to operate its business as
identified herein and to meet its obligations without the need
for substantial future capital through May 2003. There can be no
assurance that any funding mechanisms, whether identified or
not, will allow the Company to access additional funds beyond
that date.
</FONT>

December&nbsp;31, 2002. The net operating loss carryforwards
expire in the following years:

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The valuation allowance increased during 2002 and
2001 by $4,622,000 and $9,433,000, respectively, due primarily
to the increase in the net operating loss carryforward. Based on
the Internal Revenue Code and changes in the ownership of the
Company, utilization of the net operating loss carryforwards
will be subject to annual limitations.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">9.&nbsp;Leases</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The Company leases its manufacturing and office
space. Under the terms of the lease in Mount Prospect, IL, which
expires October&nbsp;2004, the Company is responsible for all
real estate taxes and operating expenses. The lease provides for
a security deposit($50,000 at December&nbsp;31, 2002) that is
secured by a certificate of deposit owned by the Company. In
addition, the Company had lease commitments for its Canadian
facility expiring August, 2004, which was subsequently broken
into two parts and successfully subleased to third parties as of
March&nbsp;1, 2003. The Company also had leased office
facilities in Dallas, through February, 2005, as of
December&nbsp;31, 2002. The Company is actively seeking
conclusion of this Dallas lease.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">10.&nbsp;401(k) Plan</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The Company has a 401(k) plan covering all
employees who meet prescribed service requirements. The plan
provides for deferred salary contributions by the plan
participants and a Company contribution. Company contributions,
if any, are at the discretion of the Board of Directors and are
not to exceed the amount deductible under applicable income tax
laws. No Company contribution was made for the years ended
December&nbsp;31, 2002, 2001, and 2000.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">11.&nbsp;Litigation</FONT></B>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Patent Litigation</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In July&nbsp;2001, the Company filed suit in the
United States District Court for the District of Delaware
against Conductus, Inc. and Superconductor Technologies, Inc.
alleging infringement of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;6,263,215,
entitled &#147;Cryoelectronically Cooled Receiver Front End for
Mobile Radio Systems&#148; (&#147;the &#146;215 patent&#148;).
This suit alleges that Conductus&#146; and Superconductor
Technologies&#146; base station front-end systems containing
cryogenically cooled superconducting filters infringe this
patent. The Company is seeking a permanent injunction enjoining
Conductus and Superconductor Technologies from marketing,
selling or manufacturing these products, as well as triple
damages and attorneys fees. Conductus and Superconductor
Technologies have denied these allegations and asked the court
to enter a judgment that the patent is invalid and not
infringed. Conductus and Superconductor Technologies are also
asserting the defense of inequitable conduct and a counterclaim
for a declaration that the patent is unenforceable. Conductus
and Superconductor Technologies have also asserted federal and
state law counterclaims, including claims of unfair competition.
Conductus and Superconductor Technologies are seeking both
compensatory and punitive damages as well as attorneys fees and
costs.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On March&nbsp;26, 2002, the Company replied to
Conductus&#146; and Superconductor Technologies&#146; Second
Amended Answer and Counterclaims and filed counterclaims
alleging that Conductus and Superconductor Technologies also
infringe U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;6,104,934 entitled
&#147;Cryoelectronic Receiver Front End&#148; and U.S. Patent
No.&nbsp;6,205,340 B1 entitled &#147;Cryoelectronic Receiver
Front End For Mobile Radio Systems&#148;. On April&nbsp;17,
2002, the court dismissed these (the Company&#146;s)
counterclaims without prejudice to the Company&#146;s right to
assert these counterclaims in a separate action.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On February&nbsp;10, 2003, the court disposed of
various motions for summary judgment filed by each party. The
court denied Superconductor Technologies&#146; motion for
summary judgment of invalidity of the &#146;215 patent as well
as Conductus&#146; motion for summary judgment limiting
computation of damages to a reasonable royalty for sales to
Dobson Communications, Inc. On Superconductor Technologies&#146;
motion for summary judgment of non-infringement, the court
granted the motion with respect to claim&nbsp;13 of the
&#146;215 patent and otherwise denied the motion with respect to
each of the other asserted claims. With regard to
Conductus&#146; motion for summary judgment of non-infringement,
the court granted the motion with respect to claim&nbsp;13 of
the &#146;215 patent and otherwise denied the motion with
respect to each of the other asserted claims. In addition, the
court denied Conductus&#146; motion for summary judgment of
invalidity of all asserted claims for causes of action existing
prior to the date of issuance of the certificate of correction
and of invalidity of claim&nbsp;13. The court also denied the
Company&#146;s motions for summary judgment that Superconductor
Technologies&#146; internal projects are not prior art to the
&#146;215 patent and to dismiss the defendants&#146;
counterclaims alleging unfair competition and interference with
business relations. The trial for this case is scheduled to
begin on March&nbsp;17, 2003. At the time of filing this
statement, the outcome of the trial was unknown.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">The Company intends to continue to prosecute
these claims vigorously against Conductus and Superconductor
Technologies and defend against counterclaims in this
litigation. The Company believes the patent to be valid, the
counterclaims asserted against the Company to be without merit,
and that it is in the best interests of the Company and its
shareholders to pursue this matter vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">48
</FONT>

<B><FONT size="2">NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">In November&nbsp;2001, the Company filed suit
against Dobson Communications, Inc. for allegedly infringing
this patent. The action has been stayed, per agreement between
the parties, until resolution of the matter between the Company
and Conductus and Superconductor Technologies. The parties have
agreed that Dobson Communications will be bound by any and all
final, non-appealable determinations, holdings or findings with
respect to all liability issues in the Company&#146;s case
against Conductus.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">Laves Litigation</FONT></B>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">On July&nbsp;17, 2000 Edward W. Laves filed an
action (the &#147;Complaint&#148;) in the Law Division of the
Circuit Court of Cook County , Illinois, against the Company and
three directors charging the Company with constructive
termination under and in breach of plaintiff&#146;s employment
agreement, and with violation of the Illinois Wage Payment and
Collection Act. Plaintiff seeks damages &#147;estimated to
exceed $12&nbsp;million.&#148; The Company filed an appearance
on behalf of all Defendants on October&nbsp;3, 2000. On
October&nbsp;6, 2000, the Company filed on Defendants&#146;
behalf a Motion to Dismiss the Complaint. On January&nbsp;22,
2001, the court issued an order granting the Company&#146;s
Motion to Dismiss the claims against the Individual Defendants,
but denied the Company&#146;s Motion to Dismiss with respect to
claims against the Company. On February&nbsp;21, 2001, Plaintiff
filed a Motion to reconsider the court&#146;s dismissal of
claims against the Individual Defendants. On March&nbsp;13,
2001, the Company filed an Answer to the Complaint and a
Memorandum in Opposition to this Motion to Reconsider. By order
dated March&nbsp;15, 2001, the court allowed Laves leave to file
an amended Motion to Reconsider, which the Plaintiff filed on
April&nbsp;5, 2001, along with a motion to dismiss one of the
Company&#146;s affirmative defenses. Following a substitution of
judges and a hearing on August&nbsp;9, 2001, the court granted
Plaintiff&#146;s motion to dismiss one of the Company&#146;s
affirmative defenses and ordered the case transferred back to
the judge originally assigned to the case for the limited
purposes of ruling on Plaintiff&#146;s amended motion to
reconsider the dismissal of claims against the Defendants. On
September&nbsp;7, 2001, following a hearing, the Judge denied
Plaintiff&#146;s amended motion to reconsider and entered an
order retaining jurisdiction of the matter for 30&nbsp;days. On
November&nbsp;9, 2001, the Judge granted Plaintiff leave to file
his First Amended Count&nbsp;II. On November&nbsp;11, 2001,
Plaintiff filed his amended pleading. On January&nbsp;31, 2002,
Plaintiff filed a corrected &#147;Unified Complaint.&#148; On
February 15, 2002, all Defendants filed their Answers to the
Unified Complaint. On March&nbsp;5, 2002, the individual
defendants served their answers to Plaintiff&#146;s
interrogatories and responses to Plaintiff&#146;s discovery
requests. On April&nbsp;8, 2002, Laves was given leave to amend
his Complaint and add Count&nbsp;III against the individual
defendants for tortious interference with contractual
obligations. Laves seeks damages against these individuals for:
(1)&nbsp;an amount to be provided at trial estimated to exceed
$12&nbsp;million; (2)&nbsp;$500,000 for Laves&#146; anxiety,
mental suffering, and humiliation; (3)&nbsp;$500,000 for
punitive damages; and (4)&nbsp;pre-and post-judgment interest
and costs. Oral fact discovery has been extended to May&nbsp;15,
2003, while all discovery is to close by August&nbsp;1, 2003.
Any &#147;dispositive&#148; motions must be filed by
July&nbsp;15, 2003. A final pre-trial will be heard on
September&nbsp;8, 2003, a week after the deadline for submission
of pretrial material. The trial is set to begin
September&nbsp;15, 2003. ISCO considers these claims without
merit and intends to defend against them vigorously.
</FONT>

<P align="left">
<B><FONT size="2">12.&nbsp;Subsequent Events</FONT></B>

<FONT size="2">The above-referenced patent suit went to trial in

expected at the end of March or beginning of April, 2003.
</FONT>

$1&nbsp;million under the uncommitted line of credit. No
warrants were issued in connection with March 2003 borrowing. Up
to 5&nbsp;million warrants may be issued in the event the
Company is authorized to borrow the $1&nbsp;million remaining
under the facility. Therefore, a maximum of 15&nbsp;million
warrants may be issued as a result of the line of credit,
presuming certain antidilutive features are not triggered.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;

Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the &#147;Exchange Act&#148;),
within 90&nbsp;days of the filing date of this Report. Based on
their evaluation, our principal executive officer and principal
accounting officer concluded that our disclosure controls and
procedures are effective.
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">There have been no significant changes (including
corrective actions with regard to significant deficiencies or
material weaknesses) in our internal controls or in other
factors that could significantly affect these controls
subsequent to the date of the evaluation referenced in paragraph
(a)&nbsp;above.

<P align="center">
<B><FONT size="2">CERTIFICATIONS</FONT></B>

<P align="left">
<FONT size="2">I, Amr Abdelmonem, certify that:
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">1.&nbsp;I have reviewed this annual report on
Form&nbsp;10-K of ISCO International, Inc.;
</FONT>

<P align="left">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
<FONT size="2">2.&nbsp;Based on my knowledge, this annual report
does not contain any untrue statement of a material fact or omit
to state a material fact necessary to make the statements made,
in light of the circumstances under which such statements were
made, not misleading with respect to the period covered by this
annual report;
</FONT>
